CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Space exploration</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Space Exploration" redirects here. For the company, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_Exploration_Technologies" title="Space Exploration Technologies">Space Exploration Technologies</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_4_Saturn_V,_s67-50531.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2369" decoding="async" height="279" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Apollo_4_Saturn_V%2C_s67-50531.jpg/220px-Apollo_4_Saturn_V%2C_s67-50531.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Apollo_4_Saturn_V%2C_s67-50531.jpg/330px-Apollo_4_Saturn_V%2C_s67-50531.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Apollo_4_Saturn_V%2C_s67-50531.jpg/440px-Apollo_4_Saturn_V%2C_s67-50531.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_4_Saturn_V,_s67-50531.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">Saturn V</a> rocket, used for the American manned lunar landing missions</div></div></div> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA00128_Moon_(18_Image_Mosaic).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2672" data-file-width="3211" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/PIA00128_Moon_%2818_Image_Mosaic%29.jpg/220px-PIA00128_Moon_%2818_Image_Mosaic%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/PIA00128_Moon_%2818_Image_Mosaic%29.jpg/330px-PIA00128_Moon_%2818_Image_Mosaic%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/PIA00128_Moon_%2818_Image_Mosaic%29.jpg/440px-PIA00128_Moon_%2818_Image_Mosaic%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA00128_Moon_(18_Image_Mosaic).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Moon as seen in a digitally processed image from data collected during the <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(spacecraft)" title="Galileo (spacecraft)"><i>Galileo</i> spacecraft flyby</a></div></div></div>\n<p><b>Space exploration</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Discovery_(observation)" title="Discovery (observation)">discovery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exploration" title="Exploration">exploration</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sky" title="Sky">celestial</a> structures in <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">outer space</a> by means of evolving and growing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_technology" title="Space technology">space technology</a>. While the study of space is carried out mainly by <a href="/wiki/Astronomer" title="Astronomer">astronomers</a> with <a href="/wiki/Telescope" title="Telescope">telescopes</a>, the physical exploration of space is conducted both by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unmanned_robotic_space_probes" title="Unmanned robotic space probes">unmanned robotic space probes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human spaceflight</a>.\n</p><p>While the observation of objects in space, known as <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, predates reliable <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">recorded history</a>, it was the development of large and relatively efficient <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">rockets</a> during the mid-twentieth century that allowed physical space exploration to become a reality. Common rationales for exploring space include advancing scientific research, national prestige, uniting different nations, ensuring the future survival of humanity, and developing military and strategic advantages against other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20150828_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20150828-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Space exploration has often been used as a proxy competition for geopolitical rivalries such as the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. The early era of space exploration was driven by a "<a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>" between the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The launch of the first human-made object to orbit <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>, the Soviet Union\'s <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik 1</a>, on 4 October 1957, and the first <a href="/wiki/Moon_landing" title="Moon landing">Moon landing</a> by the American <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">Apollo 11</a> mission on 20 July 1969 are often taken as landmarks for this initial period. The Soviet Space Program achieved many of the first milestones, including the first living being in orbit in 1957, the first <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human spaceflight</a> (<a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a> aboard <i><a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">Vostok 1</a></i>) in 1961, the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacewalk" title="Spacewalk">spacewalk</a> (by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleksei_Leonov" title="Aleksei Leonov">Aleksei Leonov</a>) on 18 March 1965, the <a href="/wiki/Luna_9" title="Luna 9">first automatic landing</a> on another celestial body in 1966, and the launch of the first <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space station</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Salyut_1" title="Salyut 1">Salyut 1</a></i>) in 1971.\nAfter the first 20 years of exploration, focus shifted from one-off flights to renewable hardware, such as the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">Space Shuttle program</a>, and from competition to cooperation as with the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> (ISS).\n</p><p>With the substantial completion of the ISS<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space-11078_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-space-11078-2">[2]</a></sup> following <a href="/wiki/STS-133" title="STS-133">STS-133</a> in March 2011, plans for space exploration by the U.S. remain in flux. <a href="/wiki/Constellation_program" title="Constellation program">Constellation</a>, a Bush Administration program for a return to the Moon by 2020<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa-163092_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa-163092-3">[3]</a></sup> was judged inadequately funded and unrealistic by <a href="/wiki/Review_of_United_States_Human_Space_Flight_Plans_Committee" title="Review of United States Human Space Flight Plans Committee">an expert review panel</a> reporting in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sm-200910_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-sm-200910-4">[4]</a></sup> \nThe Obama Administration proposed a revision of Constellation in 2010 to focus on the development of the capability for crewed missions beyond <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a> (LEO), envisioning extending the operation of the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">ISS</a> beyond 2020, transferring the development of launch vehicles for human crews from <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> to the private sector, and developing technology to enable missions to beyond LEO, such as <a href="/wiki/Lagrangian_point" title="Lagrangian point">Earth&#8211;Moon L1</a>, the Moon, <a href="/wiki/Lagrangian_point" title="Lagrangian point">Earth&#8211;Sun L2</a>, near-Earth asteroids, and <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">Phobos</a> or Mars orbit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obama_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-obama-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 2000s, the People\'s Republic of China initiated a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_space_program" title="Chinese space program">successful manned spaceflight program</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, Japan, and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> have also planned future crewed space missions. China, Russia, Japan, and India have advocated crewed missions to the Moon during the 21st century, while the European Union has advocated <a href="/wiki/Aurora_programme" title="Aurora programme">manned missions to both the Moon and Mars</a> during the 20th and 21st century.\n</p><p>From the 1990s onwards, private interests began promoting <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">space tourism</a> and then public space exploration of the Moon (see <a href="/wiki/Google_Lunar_X_Prize" title="Google Lunar X Prize">Google Lunar X Prize</a>).\n</p>\n<div class="toc" space</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-45"><a href="#Recent_and_future_developments"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Recent and future developments</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-46"><a href="#Other"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Other</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_exploration">History of exploration<span id="History"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History of exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_space_exploration" title="Timeline of space exploration">Timeline of space exploration</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_astronomy" title="History of astronomy">History of astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_first_orbital_launches_by_country" title="Timeline of first orbital launches by country">Timeline of first orbital launches by country</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Outer_space#Discovery" title="Outer space">Outer space &#167;&#160;Discovery</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atmosphere_layers-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2688" data-file-width="457" decoding="async" height="1000"
