//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Atmosphere_layers-en.svg/340px-Atmosphere_layers-en.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atmosphere_layers-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Most orbital flight actually takes place in upper layers of the atmosphere, especially in the thermosphere (not to scale)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3839" data-file-width="3500" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration.jpg/220px-Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration.jpg/330px-Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration.jpg/440px-Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration" title="Timeline of Solar System exploration">Timeline of Solar System exploration</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bumper8_launch-GPN-2000-000613.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2310" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bumper8_launch-GPN-2000-000613.jpg/220px-Bumper8_launch-GPN-2000-000613.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bumper8_launch-GPN-2000-000613.jpg/330px-Bumper8_launch-GPN-2000-000613.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bumper8_launch-GPN-2000-000613.jpg/440px-Bumper8_launch-GPN-2000-000613.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bumper8_launch-GPN-2000-000613.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In July 1950 the first <a href="/wiki/RTV-G-4_Bumper" title="RTV-G-4 Bumper">Bumper rocket</a> is launched from Cape Canaveral, Florida. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bumper_(rocket)" title="Bumper (rocket)">Bumper</a> was a two-stage rocket consisting of a Post-War <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V-2" title="V-2">V-2</a> topped by a <a href="/wiki/WAC_Corporal" title="WAC Corporal">WAC Corporal</a> rocket. It could reach then-record altitudes of almost 400&#160;km. Launched by General Electric Company, this Bumper was used primarily for testing rocket systems and for research on the upper atmosphere. They carried small payloads that allowed them to measure attributes including air temperature and cosmic ray impacts.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telescope">Telescope</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Telescope">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Telescope" title="Telescope">telescope</a> was invented in 1608 in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> by an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eyeglass" title="Eyeglass">eyeglass</a> maker named <a href="/wiki/Hans_Lippershey" title="Hans Lippershey">Hans Lippershey</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Orbiting_Astronomical_Observatory_2" title="Orbiting Astronomical Observatory 2">Orbiting Astronomical Observatory 2</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/Space_telescope" title="Space telescope">space telescope</a> launched on December 7, 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joseph_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-joseph-6">[6]</a></sup> As of February, 2nd, 2019 there are 3,891 confirmed <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_exoplanets" title="Lists of exoplanets">exoplanets</a> discovered. The <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a> is estimated to contain 100&#8211;400 billion <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">stars</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and more than 100 billion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planets" title="Planets">planets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature-20120111_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nature-20120111-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space-20130102_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Space-20130102-9">[9]</a></sup> There are at least 2 trillion <a href="/wiki/Galaxy" title="Galaxy">galaxies</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Observable_universe" title="Observable universe">observable universe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conselice_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Conselice-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20161017_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20161017-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GN-z11" title="GN-z11">GN-z11</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_most_distant_astronomical_objects" title="List of the most distant astronomical objects">most distant</a> known object from Earth, reported as 13.4 billion <a href="/wiki/Light-year" title="Light-year">light-years</a> away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assocpress20160303_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-assocpress20160303-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abcnet20160303_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-abcnet20160303-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_outer_space_flights">First outer space flights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First outer space flights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sputnik_asm.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="896" data-file-width="1094" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Sputnik_asm.jpg/220px-Sputnik_asm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Sputnik_asm.jpg/330px-Sputnik_asm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Sputnik_asm.jpg/440px-Sputnik_asm.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sputnik_asm.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik 1</a></i>, the first artificial <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> orbited Earth at 939 to 215&#160;km (583 to 134&#160;mi) in 1957, and was soon followed by <i><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_2" title="Sputnik 2">Sputnik 2</a></i>. See <a href="/wiki/Satellite#First_satellites_of_countries" title="Satellite">First satellite by country</a> (Replica Pictured)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_CSM_lunar_orbit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="904" data-file-width="1140" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Apollo_CSM_lunar_orbit.jpg/220px-Apollo_CSM_lunar_orbit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Apollo_CSM_lunar_orbit.jpg/330px-Apollo_CSM_lunar_orbit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Apollo_CSM_lunar_orbit.jpg/440px-Apollo_CSM_lunar_orbit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_CSM_lunar_orbit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Apollo CSM in lunar orbit</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2355" data-file-width="2340" decoding="async" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg/220px-Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg/330px-Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg/440px-Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">Apollo 17</a> astronaut <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Schmitt" title="Harrison Schmitt">Harrison Schmitt</a> standing next to a boulder at Taurus-Littrow.</div></div></div>\n<p>The first successful orbital launch was of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> uncrewed <i><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik 1</a></i> ("Satellite 1") mission on 4 October 1957. The satellite weighed about 83&#160;kg (183&#160;lb), and is believed to have orbited Earth at a height of about 250&#160;km (160&#160;mi). It had two radio transmitters (20 and 40&#160;MHz), which emitted "beeps" that could be heard by radios around the globe. Analysis of the radio signals was used to gather information about the electron density of the ionosphere, while temperature and pressure data was encoded in the duration of radio beeps. The results indicated that the satellite was not punctured by a <a href="/wiki/Meteoroid" title="Meteoroid">meteoroid</a>. <i>Sputnik 1</i> was launched by an <a href="/wiki/R-7_Semyorka" title="R-7 Semyorka">R-7</a> rocket. It burned up upon re-entry on 3 January 1958.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_human_outer_space_flight">First human outer space flight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: First human outer space flight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first successful human spaceflight was <i><a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">Vostok 1</a></i> ("East 1"), carrying 27-year-old Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmonaut" title="Cosmonaut">cosmonaut</a> <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a> on 12 April 1961. The spacecraft completed one orbit around the globe, lasting about 1 hour and 48 minutes. Gagarin\'s flight resonated around the world; it was a demonstration of the advanced <a href="/wiki/Soviet_space_program" title="Soviet space program">Soviet space program</a> and it opened an entirely new era in space exploration: <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human spaceflight</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_astronomical_body_space_explorations">First astronomical body space explorations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: First astronomical body space explorations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first artificial object to reach another celestial body was <a href="/wiki/Luna_2" title="Luna 2">Luna 2</a> reaching the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> in 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpl-luna2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-jpl-luna2-14">[14]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Soft_landing_(aeronautics)" title="Soft landing (aeronautics)">soft landing</a> on another celestial body was performed by <a href="/wiki/Luna_9" title="Luna 9">Luna 9</a> landing on the Moon on February 3, 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpl.luna9_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-jpl.luna9-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Luna_10" title="Luna 10">Luna 10</a> became the first artificial satellite of the Moon, entering Moon Orbit on April 3, 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpl-luna10_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-jpl-luna10-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first crewed landing on another celestial body was performed by <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">Apollo 11</a> on July 20, 1969, landing on the Moon. There have been a total of six spacecraft with humans <a href="/wiki/Moon_landing" title="Moon landing">landing on the moon</a> starting from 1969 to the last human landing in 1972.\n</p><p>The first interplanetary <a href="/wiki/Flyby_(spaceflight)" title="Flyby (spaceflight)">flyby</a> was the  1961 <a href="/wiki/Venera_1" title="Venera 1">Venera 1</a> flyby of <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a>, though the 1962 <a href="/wiki/Mariner_2" title="Mariner 2">Mariner 2</a> was the first flyby of <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a> to return data (closest approach 34,773 kilometers). <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_6,_7,_8,_and_9" title="Pioneer 6, 7, 8, and 9">Pioneer 6</a> was the first satellite to orbit the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a>, launched on December 16, 1965. The other planets were first flown by in 1965 for <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mariner_4" title="Mariner 4">Mariner 4</a>, 1973 for <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> by <i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_10" title="Pioneer 10">Pioneer 10</a></i>, 1974 for <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mariner_10" title="Mariner 10">Mariner 10</a>, 1979 for <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a> by <i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_11" title="Pioneer 11">Pioneer 11</a></i>, 1986 for <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> by <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i>, 1989 for <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a> by <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i>. In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planets</a> <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">Ceres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> were orbited by <i><a href="/wiki/Dawn_(spacecraft)" title="Dawn (spacecraft)">Dawn</a></i> and passed by <i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i>, respectively. This accounts for flybys of each of the eight planets in our <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">Ceres</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> (2 of the 5 <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet#Recognized" title="Dwarf planet">recognized dwarf planets</a>).\n</p><p>The first interplanetary surface mission to return at least limited surface data from another planet was the 1970 landing of <a href="/wiki/Venera_7" title="Venera 7">Venera 7</a> which returned data to Earth for 23 minutes from <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a>. In 1975 the <a href="/wiki/Venera_9" title="Venera 9">Venera 9</a> was the first to return images from the surface of another planet, returning images from <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a>. In 1971 the <a href="/wiki/Mars_3" title="Mars 3">Mars 3</a> mission achieved the first soft landing on Mars returning data for almost 20 seconds. Later much longer duration surface missions were achieved, including over six years of Mars surface operation by <a href="/wiki/Viking_1" title="Viking 1">Viking 1</a> from 1975 to 1982 and over two hours of transmission from the surface of Venus by <a href="/wiki/Venera_13" title="Venera 13">Venera 13</a> in 1982, the longest ever Soviet planetary surface mission. Venus and Mars are the two planets outside of Earth we have conducted surface missions on with unmanned <a href="/wiki/Robotic_spacecraft" title="Robotic spacecraft">robotic spacecraft</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_space_station">First space station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: First space station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Salyut_1" title="Salyut 1">Salyut 1</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space station</a> of any kind, launched into <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> on April 19, 1971. The <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> is currently the only fully functional space station, with continuous inhabitance since the year 2000.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_interstellar_space_flight">First interstellar space flight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: First interstellar space flight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a> became the first human-made object to <a href="/wiki/List_of_artificial_objects_leaving_the_Solar_System" title="List of artificial objects leaving the Solar System">leave our Solar System</a> into <a href="/wiki/Outer_space#Interstellar_space" title="Outer space">interstellar space</a> on August 25, 2012. The probe passed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heliopause_(astronomy)#Heliopause" title="Heliopause (astronomy)">heliopause</a> at 121 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">AU</a> to enter <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_medium" title="Interstellar medium">interstellar space</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Farthest_from_Earth">Farthest from Earth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Farthest from Earth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">Apollo 13</a> flight passed the <a href="/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon" title="Far side of the Moon">far side of the Moon</a> at an altitude of 254 kilometers (137 nautical miles) above the lunar surface, and 400,171&#160;km (248,655&#160;mi) from Earth, marking the <a href="/wiki/List_of_spaceflight_records" title="List of spaceflight records">record</a> for the farthest humans have ever traveled from Earth in 1970.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a> is currently at a distance of 145.11 astronomical units (2.1708<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>10</sup>&#160;km; 1.3489<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>10</sup>&#160;mi) (21.708 billion kilometers; 13.489 billion miles) from Earth as of January 1, 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-voyager_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-voyager-18">[18]</a></sup> It is the most distant human-made object from Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/GN-z11" title="GN-z11">GN-z11</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_most_distant_astronomical_objects" title="List of the most distant astronomical objects">most distant</a> known object from Earth, reported as 13.4 billion <a href="/wiki/Light-year" title="Light-year">light-years</a> away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assocpress20160303_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-assocpress20160303-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abcnet20160303_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-abcnet20160303-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Key_people_in_early_space_exploration">Key people in early space exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Key people in early space exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The dream of stepping into the outer reaches of Earth\'s atmosphere was driven by the fiction of <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne" title="Jules Verne">Jules Verne</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-russsw_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-russsw-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oberth_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-oberth-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa-vbbio_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa-vbbio-22">[22]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-genesis-goddard_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-genesis-goddard-23">[23]</a></sup> and rocket technology was developed to try to realize this vision. The German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V-2" title="V-2">V-2</a> was the first rocket to travel into space, overcoming the problems of thrust and material failure. During the final days of World War II this technology was obtained by both the Americans and Soviets as were its designers. The initial driving force for further development of the technology was a weapons race for intercontinental ballistic missiles (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICBM" title="ICBM">ICBMs</a>) to be used as long-range carriers for fast <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapon</a> delivery, but in 1961 when the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> launched the first man into space, the United States declared itself to be in a "<a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>" with the Soviets.\n</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Tsiolkovsky" title="Konstantin Tsiolkovsky">Konstantin Tsiolkovsky</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Goddard" title="Robert Goddard">Robert Goddard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Oberth" title="Hermann Oberth">Hermann Oberth</a></b>, and <b><a href="/wiki/Reinhold_Tiling" title="Reinhold Tiling">Reinhold Tiling</a></b> laid the groundwork of rocketry in the early years of the 20th century.\n</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Wernher_von_Braun" title="Wernher von Braun">Wernher von Braun</a></b> was the lead rocket engineer for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi" title="Nazi">Nazi</a> Germany\'s World War II <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V-2" title="V-2">V-2</a> rocket project. In the last days of the war he led a caravan of workers in the German rocket program to the American lines, where they surrendered and were brought to the United States to work on their rocket development ("<a href="/wiki/Operation_Paperclip" title="Operation Paperclip">Operation Paperclip</a>"). He acquired American citizenship and led the team that developed and launched <i><a href="/wiki/Explorer_1" title="Explorer 1">Explorer 1</a></i>, the first American satellite. Von Braun later led the team at <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">Marshall Space Flight Center</a> which developed the <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">Saturn V</a> moon rocket.\n</p><p>Initially the race for space was often led by <b><a href="/wiki/Sergei_Korolev" title="Sergei Korolev">Sergei Korolev</a></b>, whose legacy includes both the <a href="/wiki/R-7_Semyorka" title="R-7 Semyorka">R7</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_spacecraft" title="Soyuz spacecraft">Soyuz</a>&#8212;which remain in service to this day. Korolev was the mastermind behind the first satellite, first man (and first woman) in orbit and first spacewalk. Until his death his identity was a closely guarded state secret; not even his mother knew that he was responsible for creating the Soviet space program.\n</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Kerim_Kerimov" title="Kerim Kerimov">Kerim Kerimov</a></b> was one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_space_program" title="Soviet space program">Soviet space program</a> and was one of the lead architects behind the first <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human spaceflight</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">Vostok 1</a></i>) alongside Sergey Korolev. After Korolev\'s death in 1966, Kerimov became the lead scientist of the Soviet space program and was responsible for the launch of the first <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space stations</a> from 1971 to 1991, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salyut" title="Salyut">Salyut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a> series, and their precursors in 1967, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmos_186" title="Cosmos 186">Cosmos 186</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmos_188" title="Cosmos 188">Cosmos 188</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-find_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-find-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-az-1995_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-az-1995-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other key people:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Valentin_Glushko" title="Valentin Glushko">Valentin Glushko</a></b> was Chief Engine Designer for the Soviet Union. Glushko designed many of the engines used on the early Soviet rockets, but was constantly at odds with Korolev.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Vasily_Mishin" title="Vasily Mishin">Vasily Mishin</a></b> was Chief Designer working under Sergey Korolev and one of the first Soviets to inspect the captured German V-2 design. Following the death of Sergei Korolev, Mishin was held responsible for the Soviet failure to be first country to place a man on the Moon.</li>\n<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Gilruth" title="Robert Gilruth">Robert Gilruth</a></b> was the <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> head of the Space Task Force and director of 25 crewed space flights. Gilruth was the person who suggested to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> that the Americans take the bold step of reaching the Moon in an attempt to reclaim space superiority from the Soviets.</li>\n<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft,_Jr." title="Christopher C. Kraft, Jr.">Christopher C. Kraft, Jr.</a></b> was NASA\'s first <a href="/wiki/Flight_controller" title="Flight controller">flight director</a>, who oversaw development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_Control" title="Mission Control">Mission Control</a> and associated technologies and procedures.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Maxime_Faget" title="Maxime Faget">Maxime Faget</a></b> was the designer of the <a href="/wiki/Project_Mercury" title="Project Mercury">Mercury</a> capsule; he played a key role in designing the <a href="/wiki/Project_Gemini" title="Project Gemini">Gemini</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_Apollo" title="Project Apollo">Apollo</a> spacecraft, and contributed to the design of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Targets_of_exploration">Targets of exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Targets of exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Sun">The Sun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Sun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Although the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a> will probably not be physically explored at all, the study of the Sun has nevertheless been a major focus of space exploration. Being above the atmosphere in particular and Earth\'s magnetic field gives access to the solar wind and infrared and ultraviolet radiations that cannot reach Earth\'s surface. The Sun generates most <a href="/wiki/Space_weather" title="Space weather">space weather</a>, which can affect power generation and transmission systems on Earth and interfere with, and even damage, satellites and space probes. Numerous spacecraft dedicated to observing the Sun, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Telescope_Mount" title="Apollo Telescope Mount">Apollo Telescope Mount</a>, have been launched and still others have had solar observation as a secondary objective. <a href="/wiki/Parker_Solar_Probe" title="Parker Solar Probe">Parker Solar Probe</a>, launched in 2018, will approach the Sun to within 1/8th the orbit of Mercury.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mercury">Mercury</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Mercury">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before.jpg/125px-Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before.jpg/188px-Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before.jpg/250px-Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mercury_as_Never_Seen_Before.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/MESSENGER" title="MESSENGER">MESSENGER</a></i> image of Mercury (2013)</div></div></div> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:131px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MESSENGER_EN0108828359M.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1016" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/MESSENGER_EN0108828359M.png/129px-MESSENGER_EN0108828359M.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/MESSENGER_EN0108828359M.png/193px-MESSENGER_EN0108828359M.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/MESSENGER_EN0108828359M.png/258px-MESSENGER_EN0108828359M.png 2x" width="129"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MESSENGER_EN0108828359M.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <i>MESSENGER</i> image from 18,000&#160;km showing a region about 500&#160;km across (2008)</div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a> remains the least explored of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrestrial_planets" title="Terrestrial planets">Terrestrial planets</a>. As of May 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Mariner_10" title="Mariner 10">Mariner 10</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/MESSENGER" title="MESSENGER">MESSENGER</a></i> missions have been the only missions that have made close observations of Mercury. <i>MESSENGER</i> entered orbit around Mercury in March 2011, to further investigate the observations made by Mariner 10 in 1975 (Munsell, 2006b).\n</p><p>A third mission to Mercury, scheduled to arrive in 2025, <a href="/wiki/BepiColombo" title="BepiColombo">BepiColombo</a> is to include two <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">probes</a>. BepiColombo is a joint mission between Japan and the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a>. <i>MESSENGER</i> and BepiColombo are intended to gather complementary data to help scientists understand many of the mysteries discovered by Mariner 10\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gravitational_slingshot" title="Gravitational slingshot">flybys</a>.\n</p><p>Flights to other planets within the Solar System are accomplished at a cost in energy, which is described by the net change in velocity of the spacecraft, or <a href="/wiki/Delta-v" title="Delta-v">delta-v</a>. Due to the relatively high delta-v to reach Mercury and its proximity to the Sun, it is difficult to explore and orbits around it are rather unstable.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venus">Venus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Venus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Venus-real_color.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="480" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Venus-real_color.jpg/125px-Venus-real_color.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Venus-real_color.jpg/188px-Venus-real_color.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Venus-real_color.jpg/250px-Venus-real_color.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Venus-real_color.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mariner_10" title="Mariner 10">Mariner 10</a> image of Venus (1974)</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Observations_and_explorations_of_Venus" title="Observations and explorations of Venus">Observations and explorations of Venus</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a> was the first target of interplanetary flyby and lander missions and, despite one of the most hostile surface environments in the Solar System, has had more landers sent to it (nearly all from the Soviet Union) than any other planet in the Solar System. The first flyby was the 1961&#160;<a href="/wiki/Venera_1" title="Venera 1">Venera 1</a>, though the 1962&#160;<a href="/wiki/Mariner_2" title="Mariner 2">Mariner 2</a>&#160;was the first flyby&#160;to successfully return data. Mariner 2 has been followed by several other flybys by multiple space agencies often as part of missions using a Venus flyby to provide a <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">gravitational assist</a> en route to other celestial bodies. In 1967 <a href="/wiki/Venera_4" title="Venera 4">Venera 4</a> became the first probe to enter and directly examine the atmosphere of Venus. In 1970, <a href="/wiki/Venera_7" title="Venera 7">Venera 7</a> became the first successful lander to reach the surface of Venus and by 1985 it had been followed by eight additional successful Soviet Venus landers which provided images and other direct surface data. Starting in 1975 with the Soviet orbiter <a href="/wiki/Venera_9" title="Venera 9">Venera 9</a> some ten successful orbiter missions have been sent to Venus, including later missions which were able to map the surface of Venus using <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a> to pierce the obscuring atmosphere.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth">Earth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Earth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:223px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TIROS-1-Earth.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="582" data-file-width="527" decoding="async" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/TIROS-1-Earth.png/221px-TIROS-1-Earth.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/TIROS-1-Earth.png/331px-TIROS-1-Earth.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/TIROS-1-Earth.png/442px-TIROS-1-Earth.png 2x" width="221"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TIROS-1-Earth.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First television image of Earth from space, taken by <a href="/wiki/TIROS-1" title="TIROS-1">TIROS-1</a>. (1960)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3002" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/125px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/188px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/250px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Marble" title="The Blue Marble">The Blue Marble</a></i> Earth picture taken during <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">Apollo 17</a> (1972)</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Earth_observation_satellite" title="Earth observation satellite">Earth observation satellite</a></div>\n<p>Space exploration has been used as a tool to understand Earth as a celestial object in its own right. Orbital missions can provide data for Earth that can be difficult or impossible to obtain from a purely ground-based point of reference.\n</p><p>For example, the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Van_Allen_radiation_belt" title="Van Allen radiation belt">Van Allen radiation belts</a> was unknown until their discovery by the United States\' first artificial satellite, <i><a href="/wiki/Explorer_1" title="Explorer 1">Explorer 1</a></i>. These belts contain radiation trapped by Earth\'s magnetic fields, which currently renders construction of habitable space stations above 1000&#160;km impractical.\nFollowing this early unexpected discovery, a large number of Earth observation satellites have been deployed specifically to explore Earth from a space based perspective. These satellites have significantly contributed to the understanding of a variety of Earth-based phenomena. For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Ozone_depletion" title="Ozone depletion">hole in the ozone layer</a> was found by an artificial satellite that was exploring Earth\'s atmosphere, and satellites have allowed for the discovery of archeological sites or geological formations that were difficult or impossible to otherwise identify.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Moon">The Moon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: The Moon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FullMoon2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2452" data-file-width="2580" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/FullMoon2010.jpg/130px-FullMoon2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/FullMoon2010.jpg/195px-FullMoon2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/FullMoon2010.jpg/260px-FullMoon2010.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FullMoon2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> (2010)</div></div></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Moon" title="Exploration of the Moon">Exploration of the Moon</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_16_LM_Orion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2369" data-file-width="2340" decoding="async" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Apollo_16_LM_Orion.jpg/220px-Apollo_16_LM_Orion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Apollo_16_LM_Orion.jpg/330px-Apollo_16_LM_Orion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Apollo_16_LM_Orion.jpg/440px-Apollo_16_LM_Orion.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_16_LM_Orion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Apollo_16" title="Apollo 16">Apollo 16</a> LEM Orion, the <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Roving_Vehicle" title="Lunar Roving Vehicle">Lunar Roving Vehicle</a> and astronaut <a href="/wiki/John_Young_(astronaut)" title="John Young (astronaut)">John Young</a> (1972)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> was the first celestial body to be the object of space exploration. It holds the distinctions of being the first remote celestial object to be flown by, orbited, and landed upon by spacecraft, and the only remote celestial object ever to be visited by humans.\n</p><p>In 1959 the Soviets obtained the first images of the <a href="/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon" title="Far side of the Moon">far side of the Moon</a>, never previously visible to humans. The U.S. exploration of the Moon began with the <a href="/wiki/Ranger_4" title="Ranger 4">Ranger 4</a> impactor in 1962. Starting in 1966 the Soviets successfully deployed a number of <a href="/wiki/Lander_(spacecraft)" title="Lander (spacecraft)">landers</a> to the Moon which were able to obtain data directly from the Moon\'s surface; just four months later, <i><a href="/wiki/Surveyor_1" title="Surveyor 1">Surveyor 1</a></i> marked the debut of a successful series of U.S. landers. The Soviet uncrewed missions culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Lunokhod_programme" title="Lunokhod programme">Lunokhod program</a> in the early 1970s, which included the first uncrewed rovers and also successfully <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sample_return_mission" title="Sample return mission">brought lunar soil samples to Earth</a> for study. This marked the first (and to date the only) automated return of extraterrestrial soil samples to Earth. Uncrewed exploration of the Moon continues with various nations periodically deploying lunar orbiters, and in 2008 the Indian <a href="/wiki/Moon_Impact_Probe" title="Moon Impact Probe">Moon Impact Probe</a>.\n</p><p>Crewed exploration of the Moon began in 1968 with the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">Apollo 8</a> mission that successfully orbited the Moon, the first time any extraterrestrial object was orbited by humans. In 1969, the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">Apollo 11</a> mission marked the first time humans set foot upon another world. Crewed exploration of the Moon did not continue for long, however. The <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">Apollo 17</a> mission in 1972 marked the sixth landing and the most recent human visit there, and the next, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exploration_Mission_2" title="Exploration Mission 2">Exploration Mission 2</a>, is due to orbit the Moon in 2023. Robotic missions are still pursued vigorously.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mars">Mars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble.jpg/125px-Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble.jpg/188px-Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble.jpg/250px-Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_23_aug_2003_hubble.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mars, as seen by the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a> (2003)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spirit_rover_tracks.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2616" data-file-width="2957" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Spirit_rover_tracks.jpg/220px-Spirit_rover_tracks.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Spirit_rover_tracks.jpg/330px-Spirit_rover_tracks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Spirit_rover_tracks.jpg/440px-Spirit_rover_tracks.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spirit_rover_tracks.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Surface of Mars by the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover" title="Mars Exploration Rover"><i>Spirit</i> rover</a> (2004)</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">Exploration of Mars</a></div>\n<p>The exploration of <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> has been an important part of the space exploration programs of the Soviet Union (later Russia), the United States, Europe, Japan and India. Dozens of <a href="/wiki/Robotic_spacecraft" title="Robotic spacecraft">robotic spacecraft</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Orbiter" title="Orbiter">orbiters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lander_(spacecraft)" title="Lander (spacecraft)">landers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration)" title="Rover (space exploration)">rovers</a>, have been launched toward Mars since the 1960s. These missions were aimed at gathering data about current conditions and answering questions about the history of Mars. The questions raised by the scientific community are expected to not only give a better appreciation of the red planet but also yield further insight into the past, and possible future, of Earth.\n</p><p>The exploration of Mars has come at a considerable financial cost with roughly two-thirds of all spacecraft destined for Mars failing before completing their missions, with some failing before they even began. Such a high failure rate can be attributed to the complexity and large number of variables involved in an interplanetary journey, and has led researchers to jokingly speak of <i>The Great Galactic Ghoul</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space-232_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-space-232-26">[26]</a></sup> which subsists on a diet of Mars probes. This phenomenon is also informally known as the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Curse" title="Mars Curse">Mars Curse</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn-20061223_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-20061223-27">[27]</a></sup>\nIn contrast to overall high failure rates in the exploration of Mars, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> has become the first country to achieve success of its maiden attempt.  India\'s <a href="/wiki/Mars_Orbiter_Mission" title="Mars Orbiter Mission">Mars Orbiter Mission</a> (MOM)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20140924-GH_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20140924-GH-30">[30]</a></sup> is one of the least expensive interplanetary missions ever undertaken with an approximate total cost of <span style="white-space: nowrap">&#8377;</span>450 <a href="/wiki/Crore" title="Crore">Crore</a> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$73 million</span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes20131105_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes20131105-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ndtv20131105_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-ndtv20131105-32">[32]</a></sup> The first mission to Mars by any Arab country has been taken up by the United Arab Emirates. Called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emirates_Mars_Mission" title="Emirates Mars Mission">Emirates Mars Mission</a>, it is scheduled for launch in 2020. The uncrewed exploratory probe has been named "Hope Probe" and will be sent to Mars to study its atmosphere in detail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phobos">Phobos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Phobos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phobos_colour_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3300" data-file-width="3500" decoding="async" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Phobos_colour_2008.jpg/125px-Phobos_colour_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Phobos_colour_2008.jpg/188px-Phobos_colour_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Phobos_colour_2008.jpg/250px-Phobos_colour_2008.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phobos_colour_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">Phobos (moon)</a> (2008)</div></div></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Phobos" title="Exploration of Phobos">Exploration of Phobos</a></div>\n<p>The Russian space mission <a href="/wiki/Fobos-Grunt" title="Fobos-Grunt">Fobos-Grunt</a>, which launched on 9 November 2011 experienced a failure leaving it stranded in <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noburn_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-noburn-34">[34]</a></sup> It was to begin exploration of the <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">Phobos</a> and Martian circumterrestrial orbit, and study whether the moons of Mars, or at least Phobos, could be a "trans-shipment point" for spaceships traveling to Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yt-W0cUvK0Dgy8_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-yt-W0cUvK0Dgy8-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jupiter">Jupiter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Jupiter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jupiter_and_its_shrunken_Great_Red_Spot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="940" data-file-width="940" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Jupiter_and_its_shrunken_Great_Red_Spot.jpg/125px-Jupiter_and_its_shrunken_Great_Red_Spot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Jupiter_and_its_shrunken_Great_Red_Spot.jpg/188px-Jupiter_and_its_shrunken_Great_Red_Spot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Jupiter_and_its_shrunken_Great_Red_Spot.jpg/250px-Jupiter_and_its_shrunken_Great_Red_Spot.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jupiter_and_its_shrunken_Great_Red_Spot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jupiter, as seen by the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a> (2014).</div></div></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Jupiter" title="Exploration of Jupiter">Exploration of Jupiter</a></div><p>The exploration of <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> has consisted solely of a number of automated NASA spacecraft visiting the planet since 1973. A large majority of the missions have been "flybys", in which detailed observations are taken without the probe landing or entering orbit; such as in <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_program" title="Pioneer program">Pioneer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voyager_program" title="Voyager program">Voyager</a> programs. The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galileo_spacecraft" title="Galileo spacecraft">Galileo</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juno_spacecraft" title="Juno spacecraft">Juno</a></i> spacecraft are the only spacecraft to have entered the planet\'s orbit. As Jupiter is believed to have only a relatively small rocky core and no real solid surface, a landing mission is precluded.\n</p><p>Reaching Jupiter from Earth requires a delta-v of 9.2&#160;km/s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-delta-v_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-delta-v-36">[36]</a></sup> which is comparable to the 9.7&#160;km/s delta-v needed to reach low Earth orbit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pma-delta_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-pma-delta-37">[37]</a></sup> Fortunately, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gravitational_slingshot" title="Gravitational slingshot">gravity assists</a> through <a href="/wiki/Planetary_flyby" title="Planetary flyby">planetary flybys</a> can be used to reduce the energy required at launch to reach Jupiter, albeit at the cost of a significantly longer flight duration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-delta-v_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-delta-v-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Jupiter has 79 <a href="/wiki/Moons_of_Jupiter" title="Moons of Jupiter">known moons</a>, many of which have relatively little known information about them.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saturn">Saturn</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Saturn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ringworld_Waiting.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1187" data-file-width="1716" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Ringworld_Waiting.jpg/180px-Ringworld_Waiting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Ringworld_Waiting.jpg/270px-Ringworld_Waiting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Ringworld_Waiting.jpg/360px-Ringworld_Waiting.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ringworld_Waiting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A picture of Saturn taken by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cassini-Huygens" title="Cassini-Huygens">Cassini</a> (2004)</i></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Saturn" title="Exploration of Saturn">Exploration of Saturn</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:166px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Titan_Saturn_Moon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="578" data-file-width="759" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Titan_Saturn_Moon.jpg/164px-Titan_Saturn_Moon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Titan_Saturn_Moon.jpg/246px-Titan_Saturn_Moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Titan_Saturn_Moon.jpg/328px-Titan_Saturn_Moon.jpg 2x" width="164"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Titan_Saturn_Moon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view beneath the clouds of <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a>, as seen in false colour, created from a mosaic of images taken by <i><a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini&#8211;Huygens">Cassini</a></i> (2013)</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a> has been explored only through uncrewed spacecraft launched by NASA, including one mission (<i><a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini&#8211;Huygens">Cassini&#8211;Huygens</a></i>) planned and executed in cooperation with other space agencies. These missions consist of flybys in 1979 by <i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_11" title="Pioneer 11">Pioneer 11</a></i>, in 1980 by <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a></i>, in 1982 by <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i> and an orbital mission by the <i>Cassini</i> spacecraft, which lasted from 2004 until 2017.\n</p><p>Saturn has at least 62 <a href="/wiki/Moons_of_Saturn" title="Moons of Saturn">known moons</a>, although the exact number is debatable since Saturn\'s rings are made up of vast numbers of independently orbiting objects of varying sizes. The largest of the moons is <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a>, which holds the distinction of being the only moon in the Solar System with an atmosphere denser and thicker than that of Earth.  Titan holds the distinction of being the only object in the Outer Solar System that has been explored with a lander, the <i>Huygens</i> probe deployed by the <i>Cassini</i> spacecraft.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uranus">Uranus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Uranus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uranus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Uranus.jpg/125px-Uranus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Uranus.jpg/188px-Uranus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Uranus.jpg/250px-Uranus.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uranus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> as imaged by <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a> (1986)</i></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Uranus" title="Exploration of Uranus">Exploration of Uranus</a></div>\n<p>The exploration of <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> has been entirely through the <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i> spacecraft, with no other visits currently planned. Given its <a href="/wiki/Axial_tilt" title="Axial tilt">axial tilt</a> of 97.77&#176;, with its polar regions exposed to sunlight or darkness for long periods, scientists were not sure what to expect at Uranus. The closest approach to Uranus occurred on 24 January 1986. <i>Voyager 2</i> studied the planet\'s unique atmosphere and <a href="/wiki/Magnetosphere" title="Magnetosphere">magnetosphere</a>. <i>Voyager 2</i> also examined its <a href="/wiki/Rings_of_Uranus" title="Rings of Uranus">ring system</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Moons_of_Uranus" title="Moons of Uranus">moons of Uranus</a> including all five of the previously known moons, while discovering an additional ten previously unknown moons.\n</p><p>Images of Uranus proved to have a very uniform appearance, with no evidence of the dramatic storms or atmospheric banding evident on Jupiter and Saturn. Great effort was required to even identify a few clouds in the images of the planet. The magnetosphere of Uranus, however, proved to be unique, being profoundly affected by the planet\'s unusual axial tilt. In contrast to the bland appearance of Uranus itself, striking images were obtained of the Moons of Uranus, including evidence that <a href="/wiki/Miranda_(moon)" title="Miranda (moon)">Miranda</a> had been unusually geologically active.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neptune">Neptune</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Neptune">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neptune_Full.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2200" data-file-width="2200" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Neptune_Full.jpg/125px-Neptune_Full.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Neptune_Full.jpg/188px-Neptune_Full.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Neptune_Full.jpg/250px-Neptune_Full.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neptune_Full.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A picture of <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a> taken by <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a> (1989)</i></div></div></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Neptune" title="Exploration of Neptune">Exploration of Neptune</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Triton_moon_mosaic_Voyager_2_(large).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4700" data-file-width="4700" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Triton_moon_mosaic_Voyager_2_%28large%29.jpg/125px-Triton_moon_mosaic_Voyager_2_%28large%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Triton_moon_mosaic_Voyager_2_%28large%29.jpg/188px-Triton_moon_mosaic_Voyager_2_%28large%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Triton_moon_mosaic_Voyager_2_%28large%29.jpg/250px-Triton_moon_mosaic_Voyager_2_%28large%29.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Triton_moon_mosaic_Voyager_2_(large).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Triton_(moon)" title="Triton (moon)">Triton</a> as imaged by <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a> (1989)</i></div></div></div>\n<p>The exploration of Neptune began with the 25 August 1989 <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i> flyby, the sole visit to the system as of 2014. The possibility of a <a href="/wiki/Neptune_Orbiter" title="Neptune Orbiter">Neptune Orbiter</a> has been discussed, but no other missions have been given serious thought.\n</p><p>Although the extremely uniform appearance of Uranus during <i>Voyager 2</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'</span>s visit in 1986 had led to expectations that Neptune would also have few visible atmospheric phenomena, the spacecraft found that Neptune had obvious banding, visible clouds, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aurora_(astronomy)" title="Aurora (astronomy)">auroras</a>, and even a conspicuous <a href="/wiki/Great_Dark_Spot" title="Great Dark Spot">anticyclone storm system</a> rivaled in size only by Jupiter\'s small Spot. Neptune also proved to have the fastest winds of any planet in the Solar System, measured as high as 2,100&#160;km/h.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Suomi1991_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Suomi1991-38">[38]</a></sup> <i>Voyager 2</i> also examined Neptune\'s ring and moon system. It discovered 900 complete rings and additional partial ring "arcs" around Neptune. In addition to examining Neptune\'s three previously known moons, <i>Voyager 2</i> also discovered five previously unknown moons, one of which, <a href="/wiki/Proteus_(moon)" title="Proteus (moon)">Proteus</a>, proved to be the last largest moon in the system. Data from <i>Voyager 2</i> supported the view that Neptune\'s largest moon, <a href="/wiki/Triton_(moon)" title="Triton (moon)">Triton</a>, is a captured <a href="/wiki/Kuiper_belt" title="Kuiper belt">Kuiper belt</a> object.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agnor06_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Agnor06-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_objects_in_the_Solar_System">Other objects in the Solar System</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other objects in the Solar System">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nh-pluto-in-true-color_2x_JPEG-edit-frame.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Nh-pluto-in-true-color_2x_JPEG-edit-frame.jpg/125px-Nh-pluto-in-true-color_2x_JPEG-edit-frame.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Nh-pluto-in-true-color_2x_JPEG-edit-frame.jpg/188px-Nh-pluto-in-true-color_2x_JPEG-edit-frame.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Nh-pluto-in-true-color_2x_JPEG-edit-frame.jpg/250px-Nh-pluto-in-true-color_2x_JPEG-edit-frame.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nh-pluto-in-true-color_2x_JPEG-edit-frame.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i> image of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> (2015)</div></div></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pluto#Exploration" title="Pluto">Pluto &#167;&#160;Exploration</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charon_in_Color_(HQ).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Charon_in_Color_%28HQ%29.jpg/125px-Charon_in_Color_%28HQ%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Charon_in_Color_%28HQ%29.jpg/188px-Charon_in_Color_%28HQ%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Charon_in_Color_%28HQ%29.jpg/250px-Charon_in_Color_%28HQ%29.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charon_in_Color_(HQ).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i> image of <a href="/wiki/Charon_(moon)" title="Charon (moon)">Charon</a> (2015)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planet</a> Pluto  presents significant challenges for spacecraft because of its great distance from Earth (requiring high velocity for reasonable trip times) and small mass (making capture into orbit very difficult at present). <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a></i> could have visited Pluto, but controllers opted instead for a close flyby of Saturn\'s moon Titan, resulting in a trajectory incompatible with a Pluto flyby. <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i> never had a plausible trajectory for reaching Pluto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpl-faq_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-jpl-faq-40">[40]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pluto continues to be of great interest, despite its reclassification as the lead and nearest member of a new and growing class of distant icy bodies of intermediate size (and also the first member of the important subclass, defined by orbit and known as "<a href="/wiki/Plutino" title="Plutino">plutinos</a>"). After an intense political battle, a mission to Pluto dubbed <i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i> was granted funding from the United States government in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-s4p_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-s4p-41">[41]</a></sup> <i>New Horizons</i> was launched successfully on 19 January 2006. In early 2007 the craft made use of a <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">gravity assist</a> from <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>. Its closest approach to Pluto was on 14 July 2015; scientific observations of Pluto began five months prior to closest approach and continued for 16 days after the encounter.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asteroids_and_comets">Asteroids and comets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Asteroids and comets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exploration_of_the_asteroids" title="Exploration of the asteroids">Exploration of the asteroids</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_missions_to_comets" title="List of missions to comets">List of missions to comets</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Comet_Hartley_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1171" data-file-width="1683" decoding="async" height="87" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Comet_Hartley_2.jpg/125px-Comet_Hartley_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Comet_Hartley_2.jpg/188px-Comet_Hartley_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Comet_Hartley_2.jpg/250px-Comet_Hartley_2.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Comet_Hartley_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Comet <a href="/wiki/103P/Hartley" title="103P/Hartley">103P/Hartley</a> (2010)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dawn-image-070911.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Dawn-image-070911.jpg/125px-Dawn-image-070911.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Dawn-image-070911.jpg/188px-Dawn-image-070911.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Dawn-image-070911.jpg/250px-Dawn-image-070911.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dawn-image-070911.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Asteroid <a href="/wiki/4_Vesta" title="4 Vesta">4 Vesta</a>, imaged by the <a href="/wiki/Dawn_(spacecraft)" title="Dawn (spacecraft)"><i>Dawn</i> spacecraft</a> (2011)</div></div></div>\n<p>Until the advent of <a href="/wiki/Spaceflight" title="Spaceflight">space travel</a>, objects in the <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">asteroid belt</a> were merely pinpricks of light in even the largest telescopes, their shapes and terrain remaining a mystery.\nSeveral asteroids have now been visited by probes, the first of which was <i><a href="/wiki/Galileo_(spacecraft)" title="Galileo (spacecraft)">Galileo</a></i>, which flew past two: <a href="/wiki/951_Gaspra" title="951 Gaspra">951 Gaspra</a> in 1991, followed by <a href="/wiki/243_Ida" title="243 Ida">243 Ida</a> in 1993. Both of these lay near enough to <i>Galileo\'</i>s planned trajectory to Jupiter that they could be visited at acceptable cost. The first landing on an asteroid was performed by the <i><a href="/wiki/NEAR_Shoemaker" title="NEAR Shoemaker">NEAR Shoemaker</a></i> probe in 2000, following an orbital survey of the object. The dwarf planet <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">Ceres</a> and the asteroid <a href="/wiki/4_Vesta" title="4 Vesta">4 Vesta</a>, two of the three largest asteroids, were visited by NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/Dawn_(spacecraft)" title="Dawn (spacecraft)"><i>Dawn</i> spacecraft</a>, launched in 2007.\n</p><p>Although many comets have been studied from Earth sometimes with centuries-worth of observations, only a few comets have been closely visited. In 1985, the <i><a href="/wiki/International_Cometary_Explorer" title="International Cometary Explorer">International Cometary Explorer</a></i> conducted the first comet fly-by (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/21P/Giacobini-Zinner" title="21P/Giacobini-Zinner">21P/Giacobini-Zinner</a>) before joining the <a href="/wiki/Halley_Armada" title="Halley Armada">Halley Armada</a> studying the famous comet. The <a href="/wiki/Deep_Impact_(spacecraft)" title="Deep Impact (spacecraft)"><i>Deep Impact</i> probe</a> smashed into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/9P/Tempel" title="9P/Tempel">9P/Tempel</a> to learn more about its structure and composition and the <a href="/wiki/Stardust_(spacecraft)" title="Stardust (spacecraft)"><i>Stardust</i> mission</a> returned samples of another comet\'s tail. The <a href="/wiki/Philae_(spacecraft)" title="Philae (spacecraft)"><i>Philae</i> lander</a> successfully landed on <a href="/wiki/67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko" title="67P/Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko">Comet Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko</a> in 2014 as part of the broader <a href="/wiki/Rosetta_(spacecraft)" title="Rosetta (spacecraft)"><i>Rosetta</i> mission</a>.\n</p><p><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hayabusa_(spacecraft)" title="Hayabusa (spacecraft)">Hayabusa</a></i> was an <a href="/wiki/Robotic_spacecraft" title="Robotic spacecraft">unmanned spacecraft</a> developed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan_Aerospace_Exploration_Agency" title="Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency">Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sample_return_mission" title="Sample return mission">return a sample of material</a> from the small near-Earth asteroid <a href="/wiki/25143_Itokawa" title="25143 Itokawa">25143 Itokawa</a> to Earth for further analysis. Hayabusa was launched on 9 May 2003 and rendezvoused with Itokawa in mid-September 2005. After arriving at Itokawa, <i>Hayabusa</i> studied the asteroid\'s shape, spin, topography, color, composition, density, and history. In November 2005, it landed on the asteroid to collect samples. The spacecraft returned to Earth on 13 June 2010.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deep_space_exploration">Deep space exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Deep space exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Deep_space_exploration" title="Deep space exploration">Deep space exploration</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6200" data-file-width="6200" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg/220px-Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg/330px-Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg/440px-Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This high-resolution image of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hubble_Ultra_Deep_Field" title="Hubble Ultra Deep Field">Hubble Ultra Deep Field</a> includes galaxies of various ages, sizes, shapes, and colors. The smallest, reddest galaxies, are some of the most distant galaxies to have been imaged by an optical telescope.</div></div></div>\n<p>Deep space exploration is the branch of <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astronautics" title="Astronautics">astronautics</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_technology" title="Space technology">space technology</a> that is involved with the exploration of distant regions of outer space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Physical exploration of space is conducted both by <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human spaceflights</a> (deep-space astronautics) and by <a href="/wiki/Robotic_spacecraft" title="Robotic spacecraft">robotic spacecraft</a>.\n</p><p>Some of the best candidates for future deep space engine technologies include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-matter" title="Anti-matter">anti-matter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beam-powered_propulsion" title="Beam-powered propulsion">beamed propulsion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The latter, beamed propulsion, appears to be the best candidate for deep space exploration presently available, since it uses known physics and known technology that is being developed for other purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forward1996_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forward1996-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Messier51_sRGB.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Whirlpool Galaxy (Messier 51)</div></div></div>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
