role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Future_of_space_exploration" title="Future of space exploration">Future of space exploration</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Breakthrough_Starshot">Breakthrough Starshot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Breakthrough Starshot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Starshot" title="Breakthrough Starshot">Breakthrough Starshot</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Starshot" title="Breakthrough Starshot">Breakthrough Starshot</a> is a research and engineering project by the <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Initiatives" title="Breakthrough Initiatives">Breakthrough Initiatives</a> to develop a proof-of-concept fleet of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_sail" title="Light sail">light sail</a> spacecraft named <i>StarChip</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CD-20160412_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-CD-20160412-45">[45]</a></sup> to be capable of making the journey to the <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Centauri" title="Alpha Centauri">Alpha Centauri</a> star system 4.37 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light-years" title="Light-years">light-years</a> away.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_plans">Government plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Government plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the 2000s, several plans for space exploration were announced; both government entities and the private sector have space exploration objectives. China has announced plans to have a 60-ton multi-module space station in orbit by 2020.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/NASA_Authorization_Act_of_2010" title="NASA Authorization Act of 2010">NASA Authorization Act of 2010</a> provided a re-prioritized list of objectives for the American space program, as well as funding for the first priorities. NASA proposes to move forward with the development of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a> (SLS), which will be designed to carry the <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle</a>, as well as important cargo, equipment, and science experiments to Earth\'s orbit and destinations beyond. Additionally, the SLS will serve as a back up for commercial and international partner transportation services to the International Space Station. The SLS rocket will incorporate technological investments from the Space Shuttle program and the Constellation program in order to take advantage of proven hardware and reduce development and operations costs. The first developmental flight is targeted for the end of 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa-sls1_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa-sls1-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_level_automated_systems">High level automated systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: High level automated systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The idea of using high level automated systems for space missions has become a desirable goal to space agencies all around the world. Such systems are believed to yield benefits such as lower cost, less human oversight, and ability to explore deeper in space which is usually restricted by long communications with human controllers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebscohost_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-ebscohost-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomous_system">Autonomous system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Autonomous system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Autonomy is defined by three requirements:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebscohost_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-ebscohost-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ol><li>Being able to sense the world and their state, make decisions, and carry them out on their own</li>\n<li>Can interpret the given goal as a list of actions to take</li>\n<li>Fail flexibly</li></ol>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Benefits">Benefits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Benefits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Autonomous technologies would be able to perform beyond predetermined actions. They would analyze all possible states and events happening around them and come up with a safe response. In addition, such technologies can reduce launch cost and ground involvement. Performance would increase as well. Autonomy would be able to quickly respond upon encountering an unforeseen event, especially in deep space exploration where communication back to Earth would take too long.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebscohost_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-ebscohost-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="NASA.27s_Autonomous_Science_Experiment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="NASA\'s_Autonomous_Science_Experiment">NASA\'s Autonomous Science Experiment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: NASA\'s Autonomous Science Experiment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>NASA began its autonomous science experiment (ASE) on Earth Observing 1 (EO-1) which is NASA\'s first satellite in the new millennium program Earth-observing series launched on 21 November 2000. The autonomy of ASE is capable of on-board science analysis, replanning, robust execution, and later the addition of model-based diagnostic. Images obtained by the EO-1 are analyzed on-board and downlinked when a change or an interesting event occur. The ASE software has successfully provided over 10,000 science images.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebscohost_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-ebscohost-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asteroids_in_space_exploration">Asteroids in space exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Asteroids in space exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exploration_of_the_asteroids" title="Exploration of the asteroids">Exploration of the asteroids</a></div><p>An article in science magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)">Nature</a></i> suggested the use of asteroids as a gateway for space exploration, with the ultimate destination being Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-48">[48]</a></sup> In order to make such an approach viable, three requirements need to be fulfilled: first, "a thorough asteroid survey to find thousands of nearby bodies suitable for astronauts to visit"; second,  "extending flight duration and distance capability to ever-increasing ranges out to Mars"; and finally,  "developing better robotic vehicles and tools to enable astronauts to explore an asteroid regardless of its size, shape or spin."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-48">[48]</a></sup> Furthermore, using asteroids would provide astronauts with protection from galactic cosmic rays, with mission crews being able to land on them in times of greater risk to radiation exposure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rationales">Rationales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Rationales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Space_advocacy" title="Space advocacy">Space advocacy</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aldrin_Apollo_11_original.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3936" data-file-width="3912" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Aldrin_Apollo_11_original.jpg/150px-Aldrin_Apollo_11_original.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Aldrin_Apollo_11_original.jpg/225px-Aldrin_Apollo_11_original.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Aldrin_Apollo_11_original.jpg/300px-Aldrin_Apollo_11_original.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aldrin_Apollo_11_original.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Astronaut <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">Buzz Aldrin</a>, had a personal Communion service when he first arrived on the surface of the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The research that is conducted by national space exploration agencies, such as <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roscosmos" title="Roscosmos">Roscosmos</a>, is one of the reasons supporters cite to justify government expenses. Economic analyses of the NASA programs often showed ongoing economic benefits (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_spin-off" title="NASA spin-off">NASA spin-offs</a>), generating many times the revenue of the cost of the program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doi-1023_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-doi-1023-50">[50]</a></sup> It is also argued that space exploration would lead to the extraction of resources on other planets and especially asteroids, which contain billions of dollars worth of minerals and metals. Such expeditions could generate a lot of revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nature-2012_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-nature-2012-51">[51]</a></sup> As well, it has been argued that space exploration programs help inspire youth to study in science and engineering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freakonomics_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-freakonomics-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another claim is that space exploration is a necessity to mankind and that staying on Earth will lead to <a href="/wiki/Human_extinction" title="Human extinction">extinction</a>. Some of the reasons are lack of natural resources, comets, nuclear war, and worldwide epidemic. <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a>, renowned British theoretical physicist, said that "I don\'t think the human race will survive the next thousand years, unless we spread into space. There are too many accidents that can befall life on a single planet. But I\'m an optimist. We will reach out to the stars."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tele-20011016_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-tele-20011016-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>NASA has produced a series of public service announcement videos supporting the concept of space exploration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yt-EewrC22ysus_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-yt-EewrC22ysus-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Overall, the public remains largely supportive of both crewed and uncrewed space exploration. According to an <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> Poll conducted in July 2003, 71% of U.S. citizens agreed with the statement that the space program is "a good investment", compared to 21% who did not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-poll-2_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-poll-2-55">[55]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Arthur_C._Clarke" title="Arthur C. Clarke">Arthur C. Clarke</a> (1950) presented a summary of motivations for the human exploration of space in his non-fiction semi-technical monograph <i>Interplanetary Flight</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-intro-ast_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-intro-ast-56">[56]</a></sup> He argued that humanity\'s choice is essentially between expansion off Earth into space, versus cultural (and eventually biological) stagnation and death. Some analysts have even argued for creating an International Bank, exclusively to support deep space exploration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Topics">Topics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Topics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delta-Vs_for_inner_Solar_System.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1052" data-file-width="744" decoding="async" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Delta-Vs_for_inner_Solar_System.svg/220px-Delta-Vs_for_inner_Solar_System.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Delta-Vs_for_inner_Solar_System.svg/330px-Delta-Vs_for_inner_Solar_System.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Delta-Vs_for_inner_Solar_System.svg/440px-Delta-Vs_for_inner_Solar_System.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delta-Vs_for_inner_Solar_System.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Delta-v_budget" title="Delta-v budget">Delta-v\'s</a> in km/s for various orbital maneuvers</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spaceflight">Spaceflight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Spaceflight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spaceflight" title="Spaceflight">Spaceflight</a></div>\n<p><i>Spaceflight</i> is the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_technology" title="Space technology">space technology</a> to achieve the flight of <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a> into and through outer space.\n</p><p>Spaceflight is used in space exploration, and also in commercial activities like <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">space tourism</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telecommunications_satellite" title="Telecommunications satellite">satellite telecommunications</a>. Additional non-commercial uses of spaceflight include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_observatory" title="Space observatory">space observatories</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reconnaissance_satellite" title="Reconnaissance satellite">reconnaissance satellites</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Earth_observation_satellite" title="Earth observation satellite">Earth observation satellites</a>.\n</p><p>A spaceflight typically begins with a <a href="/wiki/Rocket_launch" title="Rocket launch">rocket launch</a>, which provides the initial thrust to overcome the force of <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">gravity</a> and propels the spacecraft from the surface of Earth. Once in space, the motion of a spacecraft&#8212;both when unpropelled and when under propulsion&#8212;is covered by the area of study called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astrodynamics" title="Astrodynamics">astrodynamics</a>. Some spacecraft remain in space indefinitely, some disintegrate during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_reentry" title="Atmospheric reentry">atmospheric reentry</a>, and others reach a planetary or lunar surface for landing or impact.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellites">Satellites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Satellites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">Satellite</a></div>\n<p>Satellites are used for a large number of purposes. Common types include military (spy) and civilian Earth observation satellites, communication satellites, navigation satellites, weather satellites, and research satellites. <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">Space stations</a> and human <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a> in orbit are also satellites.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercialization_of_space">Commercialization of space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Commercialization of space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commercialization_of_space" title="Commercialization of space">Commercialization of space</a></div>\n<p>Current examples of the commercial use of space include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satellite_navigation_system" title="Satellite navigation system">satellite navigation systems</a>, satellite television and <a href="/wiki/Satellite_radio" title="Satellite radio">satellite radio</a>. <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">Space tourism</a> is the recent phenomenon of <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">space travel</a> by individuals for the purpose of personal pleasure.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">Private spaceflight companies</a> such as <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blue_Origin" title="Blue Origin">Blue Origin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Orbital_Technologies_Commercial_Space_Station" title="Orbital Technologies Commercial Space Station">commercial space stations</a> such as the Axiom Space and the <a href="/wiki/Bigelow_Commercial_Space_Station" title="Bigelow Commercial Space Station">Bigelow Commercial Space Station</a> have dramatically changed the landscape of space exploration, and will continue to do so in the near future.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alien_life">Alien life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Alien life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Astrobiology" title="Astrobiology">Astrobiology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">Extraterrestrial life</a></div>\n<p>Astrobiology is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interdisciplinary" title="Interdisciplinary">interdisciplinary</a> study of life in the universe, combining aspects of <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a> and geology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAastrobio_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAastrobio-59">[59]</a></sup> It is focused primarily on the study of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Origin_of_life" title="Origin of life">origin</a>, distribution and <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolution</a> of life. It is also known as <b>exobiology</b> (from Greek: &#941;&#958;&#969;, <i>exo</i>, "outside").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aleph-x_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-aleph-x-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www-pho_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-www-pho-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-itw-1066_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-itw-1066-62">[62]</a></sup>  The term "Xenobiology" has been used as well, but this is technically incorrect because its terminology means "biology of the foreigners".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bio-ast_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-bio-ast-63">[63]</a></sup>  Astrobiologists must also consider the possibility of life that is chemically entirely distinct from any life found on Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AstroDNA_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-AstroDNA-64">[64]</a></sup> In the Solar System some of the prime locations for current or past astrobiology are on Enceladus, Europa, Mars, and Titan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sc-extra_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-sc-extra-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Living_in_space">Living in space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Living in space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Space_colonization" title="Space colonization">Space colonization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Space_habitat" title="Space habitat">Space habitat</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_Station" title="Space Station">Space Station</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S122e008264.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/S122e008264.jpg/220px-S122e008264.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/S122e008264.jpg/330px-S122e008264.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/S122e008264.jpg/440px-S122e008264.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S122e008264.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Module" title="Columbus Module">Columbus Module</a> at the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>, launched into space on the US Space Shuttle mission <a href="/wiki/STS-122" title="STS-122">STS-122</a> in 2008</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bernal_sphere_interior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4247" data-file-width="5716" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Bernal_sphere_interior.jpg/350px-Bernal_sphere_interior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Bernal_sphere_interior.jpg/525px-Bernal_sphere_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Bernal_sphere_interior.jpg/700px-Bernal_sphere_interior.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bernal_sphere_interior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Artist\'s conception of the interior of a <a href="/wiki/Bernal_sphere" title="Bernal sphere">Bernal sphere</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Space colonization, also called space settlement and space humanization, would be the permanent autonomous (self-sufficient) human <a href="/wiki/Space_habitat" title="Space habitat">habitation</a> of locations outside Earth, especially of natural satellites or planets such as the <a href="/wiki/Colonization_of_the_Moon" title="Colonization of the Moon">Moon</a> or <a href="/wiki/Colonization_of_Mars" title="Colonization of Mars">Mars</a>, using significant amounts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-situ_resource_utilization" title="In-situ resource utilization">in-situ resource utilization</a>.\n</p><p>To date, the longest human occupation of space is the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> which has been in continuous use for 18&#160;years, 108&#160;days. <a href="/wiki/Valeri_Polyakov" title="Valeri Polyakov">Valeri Polyakov</a>\'s record single spaceflight of almost 438 days aboard the <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a> space station has not been surpassed. Long-term stays in space reveal issues with bone and muscle loss in low gravity, immune system suppression, and radiation exposure.\n</p><p>Many past and current concepts for the continued exploration and colonization of space focus on a return to the Moon as a "stepping stone" to the other planets, especially Mars. At the end of 2006 NASA announced they were planning to build a permanent Moon base with continual presence by 2024.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa-164021_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa-164021-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Beyond the technical factors that could make living in space more widespread, it has been suggested that the lack of <a href="/wiki/Private_property" title="Private property">private property</a>, the inability or difficulty in establishing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Property_rights" title="Property rights">property rights</a> in space, has been an impediment to the development of space for human habitation. Since the advent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_technology" title="Space technology">space technology</a> in the latter half of the twentieth century, the ownership of property in space has been murky, with strong arguments both for and against. In particular, the making of <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">national</a> <a href="/wiki/Land_claim" title="Land claim">territorial claims</a> in <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">outer space</a> and on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celestial_body" title="Celestial body">celestial bodies</a> has been specifically proscribed by the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Space_Treaty" title="Outer Space Treaty">Outer Space Treaty</a>, which had been, as of  2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, ratified by all <a href="/wiki/Spacefaring" title="Spacefaring">spacefaring nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tna2012fall_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-tna2012fall-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RocketSunIcon.svg/28px-RocketSunIcon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RocketSunIcon.svg/42px-RocketSunIcon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RocketSunIcon.svg/56px-RocketSunIcon.svg.png 2x" width="28"/></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Spaceflight" title="Portal:Spaceflight">Spaceflight portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_space_exploration" title="Outline of space exploration">Outline of space exploration</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner"
